# full-rds-example

 This is example illustrate a real case on AWS, regarding the needs of a fake application. The key points are : 

 * Deploy a VPC where all our resources will be deployed.
 * Deploy a Postgresql RDS Instance (publicly accessible but restricted to our personal Outbound IP Address).
 * Deploy the postgresql database users needed for the fake application.
 * All user's passwords will be generated at-fly and stored into AWS SecretsManager.
 * Deploy Real-time audit system with pgaudit extension.
 * Deploy an ElasticSearch domain to index logs produced by pgaudit extension.

This example will show you the principe of `least privilege` applied to the database users used by the application.

 ## Fake Application

Imagine an application that manages basket for their customers. the database relational database is represented by this diagram :

This application is divded into 3 differents components : 

* a **web component** that needs the permissions "write" on customer and basket tables. It needs too the permissions "read" on product table.
* a **backoffice component** that in charge to update product items and price. It needs only "read" permissions on customer and basket tables.
* a **batch component** that in charge to create statistics in table stats from others tables. This batch will be implemented by an unbelievable plsql procedure ! The batch need "read" permissions on customer,product,basket tables and "write" permissions on stats table.

|Component| CUSTOMER | BASKET | PRODUCT | STATS |
|---------|----------|--------------|----------------|-----------|
|Web|Write Operations|Write Operations|Read Operations|N/A|
|BackOffice|Read Operations|Read Operations|Write Operations|N/A|
|Stats|Read Operations|Read Operations|Read Operations|Write Operations|


Before starting, you need to prepare your environment by setting variables. You can used the excellent library [direnv](https://direnv.net/). This is the content of the `.envrc` file : 

```
export PGPASSWORD="My-Strong-Password"
export AWS_PROFILE=your-aws-profile
export TF_VAR_rds_root_password="${PGPASSWORD}"
```

|Variable|Description|
|-----------|---------------|
|PGPASSWORD|Native PostgreSQL environment variable. Used by the postgresql provider.|
|AWS_PROFILE|AWS Profile providing authentication informations on your AWS Account.|
|TF_VAR_rds_root_password| Value for terraform variable `rds_root_password`. |

Terraform providers are defined into the `providers.tf` file.

## Step 1 - Deploy our playground

You can find all the required code in the file `vpc.tf`.

> Note that, it's a demonstration usecase. So the VPC settings does not cover `cloudtrail` or `vpc flow logs`.

In the `terraform.tfvars`, you could find the value used to configure the vpc : 

```hcl
# a standard vpc
vpc_cidr = "10.66.0.0/18"

vpc_public_subnets   = ["10.66.0.0/24", "10.66.1.0/24", "10.66.2.0/24"]
vpc_private_subnets  = ["10.66.3.0/24", "10.66.4.0/24", "10.66.5.0/24"]
vpc_database_subnets = ["10.66.6.0/24", "10.66.7.0/24", "10.66.8.0/24"]
```

In the `vpc.tf` file, you will find too a `security_group` for our RDS Instance that will be used to restrict access on our personal Outbound IP Address. 


## Step 2 - Deploy our RDS Instance

We use the offical terraform module to deploy our RDS Instance. The code is available in the file `rds.tf`.

```hcl
######################################
# Deploy RDS Instance
######################################
module "rds" {
  source  = "terraform-aws-modules/rds/aws"
  version = "3.5.0"

  identifier = local.name

  # All available versions: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/CHAP_PostgreSQL.html#PostgreSQL.Concepts
  engine               = "postgres"
  engine_version       = var.rds_engine_version
  family               = var.rds_family
  major_engine_version = var.rds_major_engine_version
  instance_class       = var.rds_instance_class

  allocated_storage     = var.rds_allocated_storage
  max_allocated_storage = var.rds_max_allocated_storage
  storage_encrypted     = var.rds_storage_encrypted

  # NOTE: Do NOT use 'user' as the value for 'username' as it throws:
  # "Error creating DB Instance: InvalidParameterValue: MasterUsername
  # user cannot be used as it is a reserved word used by the engine"
  name     = var.inputs["db_name"]
  username = var.rds_superuser_name
  # password is setted inside environment variable TF_VAR_rds_root_password
  password = var.rds_root_password
  port     = 5432

  multi_az = true

  # because we want reach the database from our local workstation, we need to deploy our RDS in the public subnets
  # DO NOT DO THAT IN PRODUCTION
  # to reduce the attack surface, limit the access of the RDS Instance to our personal IP addresses
  publicly_accessible    = true
  subnet_ids             = module.vpc.public_subnets
  vpc_security_group_ids = [module.security_group.security_group_id]

  maintenance_window              = "Mon:00:00-Mon:03:00"
  backup_window                   = "03:00-06:00"
  enabled_cloudwatch_logs_exports = ["postgresql", "upgrade"]

  backup_retention_period = 0
  skip_final_snapshot     = true
  deletion_protection     = false # for test purpose !!

  create_db_parameter_group = false
  parameter_group_name      = aws_db_parameter_group.postgres.id

  create_db_option_group = false

  create_db_subnet_group = false
  db_subnet_group_name   = aws_db_subnet_group.main_db_subnet_group.id

  tags = local.tags
}
```

And settings of our RDS are available in the `terraform.tfvars` : 

```hcl
# rds settings
rds_name                  = "myfullrdsexample"
rds_engine_version        = "13.5"
rds_major_engine_version  = "13"
rds_family                = "postgres13"
rds_instance_class        = "db.t3.micro"
rds_allocated_storage     = 10
rds_max_allocated_storage = 20
allowed_ip_addresses      = ["X.X.X.X/32"] # your personal Outbound IP Address
rds_superuser_name        = "root"
```

> Note : we rename the super-user in `root`. 

> Replace the `allowed_ip_addresses` with your personal Outbound IP address. use `curl ifconfig.me` to retrieve it.

## Step 3 - Deploy the admin user of our Database

You could find the code in the `postgresql.tf` file. There is 2 phases here : 

### Deploy Roles and Permissions

We use the **create-database** submodule to deploy roles and permissions : 

```hcl
########################################
# Initialize the database and the objects 
# (roles & grants), the default privileges
########################################
module "initdb" {

  source  = "jparnaudeau/database-admin/postgresql//create-database"
  version = "2.0.1"

  depends_on = [module.rds]

  # set the provider
  providers = {
    postgresql = postgresql.pgadm
  }

  # targetted rds
  pgadmin_user = var.rds_superuser_name
  dbhost       = module.rds.db_instance_address
  dbport       = var.dbport

  # input parameters for creating database & objects inside database
  create_database = false
  inputs          = var.inputs

  # because the superuser is not "postgres", need to set it in the module
  default_superusers_list = [var.rds_superuser_name]
}
```

> Note : we pass `false` to the argument `create_database` because the database will already been created at the previous step.

and the settings in the terraform.tfvars :

```hcl
# database and objects creation
inputs = {

  # parameters used for creating database
  db_schema_name = "public"
  db_name        = "mydatabase"     # should be the same as var.rds_name. if not, a new database will be created
  db_admin       = "app_admin_role" #owner of the database

  # install extensions if needed
  extensions = ["pgaudit"]

  # CREATE ROLE
  db_roles = [
    { id = "admin", role = "app_admin_role", inherit = true, login = false, validity = "infinity", privileges = ["USAGE", "CREATE"], createrole = true },
  ],

  #  GRANT PERMISSIONS ON ROLES
  db_grants = [
    # define grants for app_admin_role : 
    # - access to all objects on database
    { object_type = "database", privileges = ["CREATE", "CONNECT", "TEMPORARY"], objects = [], role = "app_admin_role", owner_role = "root", grant_option = true },
    { object_type = "type", privileges = ["USAGE"], objects = [], role = "app_admin_role", owner_role = "root", grant_option = true },

  ],

  # CREATE USER
  db_users = [
    { name = "admin", inherit = true, login = true, membership = ["app_admin_role"], validity = "infinity", connection_limit = -1, createrole = true },
  ]

}

# Refresh or not refresh passwords
refresh_passwords = ["all"]
```

> **db_roles** : this structure deploys roles. Note the `create_role` attribut that give the permission to create role and set permissions on it. It's a very high level of permissions and it should give only for administration role.

> **db_grants** : This structure wraps the primitive [**postgresql_grant**](https://registry.terraform.io/providers/cyrilgdn/postgresql/latest/docs/resources/postgresql_grant) provided by the postgresql provider.

> **role** and **owner_role** : `role` are the role on which we want set permissions. `owner_role` is the role that apply the sql command to grant permissions. So, here, it's the super-user `root` because the admin user does not exists yet.

> **objects = []** : It's with this attribut that we can manage fine-grained permissions on table. set to `[]` means **all**.


### Deploy admin user

We use the **create-users** submodule to deploy users that will inherits permissions from previous roles : 

```
#########################################
# Create the users inside the database
#########################################
# AWS Region
data "aws_region" "current" {}

module "create_users" {
  source  = "jparnaudeau/database-admin/postgresql//create-users"
  version = "2.0.1"

  # need that all objects, managed inside the module "initdb", are created
  depends_on = [module.initdb]

  # set the provider
  providers = {
    postgresql = postgresql.pgadm
  }

  # targetted rds
  pgadmin_user = var.rds_superuser_name
  dbhost       = module.rds.db_instance_address
  dbport       = var.dbport

  # input parameters for creating users inside database
  db_users = var.inputs["db_users"]

  # set passwords
  passwords = { for user in var.inputs["db_users"] : user.name => random_password.passwords[user.name].result }

  # set postprocessing playbook
  postprocessing_playbook_params = {
    enable  = true
    db_name = var.inputs["db_name"]
    extra_envs = {
      REGION   = data.aws_region.current.name
      RDS_NAME = var.rds_name
    }
    refresh_passwords = var.refresh_passwords
    shell_name        = "./gen-password-in-secretsmanager.py"
  }
}
```

> **db_users** : the structure provides the list of users. in Postgresql model, users are `role` with the attribut `login = true`. Refer to [**postgresql_role**](https://registry.terraform.io/providers/cyrilgdn/postgresql/latest/docs/resources/postgresql_role) for details of the primitive.

> passwords are initialized with a `random_password` resource. Those passwords will be replaced during post-processing playbook execution.

> The post-processing playbook is implemented with the `gen-password-in-secretsmanager.py`. This script will generate a random password, set this password to the user in database, and store it into AWS SecretsManager.

> in terraform.tfvars, the attribut `refresh_passwords = ["all"]` indicates that each time the terraform is applied, the post-processing playbook is executed, and a new password is setted for each user.

> At opposite, `refresh_passwords = [""]` can avoid the password recreation.

> If you want rotate the password of a particular user (by example johndoe), set `refresh_passwords = ["johndoe"]`

## Time to apply

Ok. You can apply the terraform code. Take a coffee, it takes 20 minutes at least to deploy all resources. At the end, you will have something like this : 

```
Apply complete! Resources: 44 added, 0 changed, 0 destroyed.

Outputs:

affected_schema = "public"
created_roles = [
  "app_admin_role",
]
db_users = {
  "admin" = {
    "connect_command" = "psql -h myfullrdsexample.psg1madrid0.eu-west-3.rds.amazonaws.com -p 5432 -U admin -d mydatabase -W"
    "secret_arn" = "arn:aws:secretsmanager:eu-west-3:444444444444:secret:secret-kv-myfullrdsexample-admin-PFxvvF"
    "secret_name" = "secret-kv-myfullrdsexample-admin"
  }
}
```

Trying to connect to our database :

```bash
psql -h myfullrdsexample.psg1madrid0.eu-west-3.rds.amazonaws.com -p 5432 -U admin -d mydatabase -W
Password: <find password in AWS SecretsManager in secret-kv-myfullrdsexample-admin>
psql (13.5 (Ubuntu 13.5-2.pgdg20.04+1))
SSL connection (protocol: TLSv1.2, cipher: ECDHE-RSA-AES256-GCM-SHA384, bits: 256, compression: off)
Type "help" for help.

mydatabase=> \l
                                     List of databases
    Name    |  Owner   | Encoding |   Collate   |    Ctype    |     Access privileges
------------+----------+----------+-------------+-------------+----------------------------
 mydatabase | root     | UTF8     | en_US.UTF-8 | en_US.UTF-8 | =Tc/root                  +
            |          |          |             |             | root=CTc/root             +
            |          |          |             |             | app_admin_role=C*T*c*/root
 postgres   | root     | UTF8     | en_US.UTF-8 | en_US.UTF-8 |
 rdsadmin   | rdsadmin | UTF8     | en_US.UTF-8 | en_US.UTF-8 | rdsadmin=CTc/rdsadmin     +
            |          |          |             |             | rdstopmgr=Tc/rdsadmin
 template0  | rdsadmin | UTF8     | en_US.UTF-8 | en_US.UTF-8 | =c/rdsadmin               +
            |          |          |             |             | rdsadmin=CTc/rdsadmin
 template1  | root     | UTF8     | en_US.UTF-8 | en_US.UTF-8 | =c/root                   +
            |          |          |             |             | root=CTc/root
(5 rows)
```


## Step 4 - Deploy tables and procedure.

To create roles and permissions with fine-grained permissions, because we can't apply permissions on inexistent tables, we need to create it first. 

```
psql -h myfullrdsexample.psg1madrid0.eu-west-3.rds.amazonaws.com -p 5432 -U admin -d mydatabase -f create-tables.sql -W
Password: <find password in AWS SecretsManager in secret-kv-myfullrdsexample-admin>
CREATE TABLE
INSERT 0 1
CREATE TABLE
CREATE INDEX
CREATE TABLE
CREATE TABLE

psql -h myfullrdsexample.psg1madrid0.eu-west-3.rds.amazonaws.com -p 5432 -U admin -d mydatabase -f create-procedure-statistiques.sql -W

mydatabase=> \dt
         List of relations
 Schema |   Name   | Type  | Owner
--------+----------+-------+-------
 public | basket   | table | admin
 public | customer | table | admin
 public | product  | table | admin
 public | stats    | table | admin
(4 rows)

```

## Step 5 - Deploy roles, permissions and users for our application.

In the example directory, you could find the file `terraform.tfvars.step5`. It contains the new values for `var.inputs`. 

Rename terraform.tfvars to terraform.tfvars.step1, report any modifications that you have made into terraform.tfvars.step5 and rename it in terraform.tfvars.

the new `var.inputs` is : 

### Roles

```
  # ---------------------------------- ROLES ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  # In this example, we want illustrate the "least privilege pattern". We have a schema in which 4 tables have been created : Customer, Product, Basket, Stats
  # We will create 4 roles :
  # - "app_admin_role" will be the role used for creation, deletion, grant operations on objects etc .. It's the "admin" role used for managed objects inside db 'mydatabase' (var.inputs['db_name']), schema 'public'
  # - "app_readonly_role" for readonly operations.
  # - "app_writeweb_role" for operations allowed from "web" application.
  # - "app_writebo_role" for operations allowed from "backoffice" application.
  db_roles = [
    { id = "admin", role = "app_admin_role", inherit = true, login = false, validity = "infinity", privileges = ["USAGE", "CREATE"], createrole = true },
    { id = "readonly", role = "app_readonly_role", inherit = true, login = false, validity = "infinity", privileges = ["USAGE"], createrole = false },
    { id = "web", role = "app_writeweb_role", inherit = true, login = false, validity = "infinity", privileges = ["USAGE"], createrole = false },
    { id = "backoffice", role = "app_writebo_role", inherit = true, login = false, validity = "infinity", privileges = ["USAGE"], createrole = false },
    { id = "batch", role = "app_writebatch_role", inherit = true, login = false, validity = "infinity", privileges = ["USAGE"], createrole = false },
  ],

```

### Permissions

```

  # ---------------------------------- GRANT PERMISSIONS ON ROLES ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  # Notes : 
  #   - "role" corresponds to the role on which the grants will be applied.
  #   - "owner_role" is the role used to create grants on "role".
  #   - object_type = "type" is used only for default privileges
  #   - objects = [] means "all"
  # all these grants are related to db 'mydatabase' (var.inputs['db_name']), schema 'public' (var.inputs['db_schema_name'])
  db_grants = [

    # define grants for app_admin_role : 
    # - access to all objects on database
    { object_type = "database", privileges = ["CREATE", "CONNECT", "TEMPORARY"], objects = [], role = "app_admin_role", owner_role = "root", grant_option = true },
    { object_type = "type", privileges = ["USAGE"], objects = [], role = "app_admin_role", owner_role = "root", grant_option = true },


    # define grants for app_readonly_role
    # - access to 'SELECT' on all tables 
    # - access to 'SELECT' on all sequences
    { object_type = "database", privileges = ["CONNECT"], objects = [], role = "app_readonly_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "type", privileges = ["USAGE"], objects = [], role = "app_readonly_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "table", privileges = ["SELECT", "REFERENCES", "TRIGGER"], objects = [], role = "app_readonly_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "sequence", privileges = ["SELECT", "USAGE"], objects = [], role = "app_readonly_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },


    # define grants for app_writeweb_role
    # - access in Read/Write on tables "customer" & "basket"
    # - access in Read on table "Product"
    { object_type = "database", privileges = ["CONNECT"], objects = [], role = "app_writeweb_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "type", privileges = ["USAGE"], objects = [], role = "app_writeweb_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "table", privileges = ["SELECT", "REFERENCES", "TRIGGER", "INSERT", "UPDATE", "DELETE"], objects = ["customer", "basket"], role = "app_writeweb_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "table", privileges = ["SELECT", "REFERENCES", "TRIGGER"], objects = ["product"], role = "app_writeweb_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "sequence", privileges = ["SELECT", "USAGE"], objects = [], role = "app_writeweb_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "function", privileges = ["EXECUTE"], objects = [], role = "app_writeweb_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },


    # define grants for app_writebo_role
    # - access in Read/Write on table "product"
    # - access in Read on table "customer", "basket", "stats"
    { object_type = "database", privileges = ["CONNECT"], objects = [], role = "app_writebo_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "type", privileges = ["USAGE"], objects = [], role = "app_writebo_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "table", privileges = ["SELECT", "REFERENCES", "TRIGGER", "INSERT", "UPDATE", "DELETE"], objects = ["product"], role = "app_writebo_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "table", privileges = ["SELECT", "REFERENCES", "TRIGGER"], objects = ["customer", "basket", "stats"], role = "app_writebo_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "sequence", privileges = ["SELECT", "USAGE"], objects = [], role = "app_writebo_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "function", privileges = ["EXECUTE"], objects = [], role = "app_writebo_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },


    # define grants for app_writebatch_role
    # - access in Read/Write on table "stats"
    # - access in Read on table "customer", "basket", "product"
    { object_type = "database", privileges = ["CONNECT"], objects = [], role = "app_writebatch_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "type", privileges = ["USAGE"], objects = [], role = "app_writebatch_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "table", privileges = ["SELECT", "REFERENCES", "TRIGGER", "INSERT", "UPDATE", "DELETE"], objects = ["stats"], role = "app_writebatch_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "table", privileges = ["SELECT", "REFERENCES", "TRIGGER"], objects = ["customer", "basket", "product"], role = "app_writebatch_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "sequence", privileges = ["SELECT", "USAGE"], objects = [], role = "app_writebatch_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },
    { object_type = "function", privileges = ["EXECUTE"], objects = [], role = "app_writebatch_role", owner_role = "app_admin_role", grant_option = false },

  ],

```

> As you can see, we could create several permissions on `table` object_type. 

> Note that for each line, the `owner_role` is the `app_admin_role` and not the super-user as we do in the previous step.

### Users

```
  db_users = [
    { name = "admin", inherit = true, login = true, membership = ["app_admin_role"], validity = "infinity", connection_limit = -1, createrole = true },
    { name = "web", inherit = true, login = true, membership = ["app_writeweb_role"], validity = "infinity", connection_limit = -1, createrole = false },
    { name = "backoffice", inherit = true, login = true, membership = ["app_writebo_role"], validity = "infinity", connection_limit = -1, createrole = false },
    { name = "batch", inherit = true, login = true, membership = ["app_writebatch_role"], validity = "infinity", connection_limit = -1, createrole = false },
    { name = "lemmy", inherit = true, login = true, membership = ["app_readonly_role"], validity = "2022-07-31 00:00:00+00", connection_limit = -1, createrole = false },
  ]

}

# Refresh or not refresh passwords
refresh_passwords = ["web","backoffice","batch","lemmy"]
```

> We create a human user `lemmy` that have read-only permissions on all tables and with an expiration date.

> We limit the `refresh_passwords` list to the new users. It avoid to rotate the password of the admin user created in the previous step.

> To disable a user without delete it, pass the attribut `login` to `false`.

Relaunch the apply. At the end, you will have your users ready to be used in the application.

This the results of the test : 

* user **backoffice** : 

|Operation | Customer | Basket | Product | Stats |
|--------------|---------------|-----------|------------|-------|
| Read|OK | OK | OK | OK |
|Write|Permission Denied | Permission Denied | OK |Permission Denied|

* user **web** :

|Operation | Customer | Basket | Product | Stats |
|--------------|---------------|-----------|------------|-------|
| Read|OK | OK | OK | Permission Denied |
|Write|OK | OK | Permission Denied |Permission Denied|

* user **batch** : 

|Operation | Customer | Basket | Product | Stats |
|--------------|---------------|-----------|------------|-------|
| Read|OK | OK | OK | OK |
|Write|Permission Denied | Permission Denied | Permission Denied |OK|

Let's try to hack the system with the user `web` : 

```
psql -h myfullrdsexample.psg1madrid0.eu-west-3.rds.amazonaws.com -p 5432 -U web -d mydatabase -W
Password:
psql (13.5 (Ubuntu 13.5-2.pgdg20.04+1))
SSL connection (protocol: TLSv1.2, cipher: ECDHE-RSA-AES256-GCM-SHA384, bits: 256, compression: off)

mydatabase=> CREATE DATABASE exfiltration;
ERROR:  permission denied to create database

mydatabase=> CREATE SCHEMA exfiltration;
ERROR:  permission denied for database mydatabase

mydatabase=> CALL feed_stats(1);
ERROR:  permission denied for table stats
CONTEXT:  SQL statement "insert into stats (product,value) values (infos.ProductLabel,infos.totalAmount)"
PL/pgSQL function feed_stats(integer) line 18 at SQL statement

mydatabase=> CREATE ROLE dream SUPERUSER LOGIN PASSWORD 'theater';
ERROR:  must be superuser to create superusers

mydatabase=> CREATE ROLE suicidal CREATEDB LOGIN PASSWORD 'tendencies';
ERROR:  permission denied to create role

mydatabase=> CREATE ROLE marilyn LOGIN PASSWORD 'manson';
ERROR:  permission denied to create role

mydatabase=> CREATE ROLE slayer;
ERROR:  permission denied to create role
```

> Important Note : As explained in the Readme of the module, if you create new tables after the `terraform apply`, for `write` or `read` permissions for all tables (`objects=[]`), you need to re-apply the terraform to propagate the permissions on the new tables. Otherwise, you will encount `Permission Denied`. The grants **are not retro-active**.

## Optional : real-time Audit 

In some usecase, you need to set up an audit system to prove the queries executed on certain tables.. This particular aspect is covered by the pg_extension [`pg_audit`](https://github.com/pgaudit/pgaudit).

AWS RDS Instance supports this pg_extension. To activate it, go to the terraform.tfvars : 

```
# install extensions if needed
extensions = ["pgaudit"]
```

Create the pg_extension is not enough. You need to pass an `aws_db_parameter_group` to your RDS Instance. This is already the case in this example. Look in the `rds.tf` file : 

```
######################################
# Deploy RDS Instance
######################################
module "rds" {
  source  = "terraform-aws-modules/rds/aws"
  version = "3.5.0"

  ...

  create_db_parameter_group = false
  parameter_group_name      = aws_db_parameter_group.postgres.id

  ...
}

resource "aws_db_parameter_group" "postgres" {
  name        = format("param-%s-%s", local.name, random_id.val.hex)
  description = "Parameter group for our postgresql rds instance"
  family      = var.rds_family

  dynamic "parameter" {
    for_each = var.parameter_group_params["immediate"]
    content {
      name  = parameter.key
      value = parameter.value
    }
  }
  dynamic "parameter" {
    for_each = var.parameter_group_params["pending-reboot"]
    content {
      name         = parameter.key
      value        = parameter.value
      apply_method = "pending-reboot"
    }
  }

  tags = local.tags
}
```

pg_extension needs specific parameters to be pass in the configuration of your postgresql server. This is done inside the `aws_db_parameter_group`. Look in the terraform.tfvars : 

```
# define parameter groups for our RDS, apply_method = "immediate"
# for setting pg_extension parameters, the apply_method need to be "pending-reboot"
# reboot required if the database already exsits : aws rds reboot-db-instance --db-instance-identifier xxx
# extension pg_stat_statements : https://pganalyze.com/docs/install/amazon_rds/01_configure_rds_instance
# extension pg_audit           : https://aws.amazon.com/premiumsupport/knowledge-center/rds-postgresql-pgaudit/?nc1=h_ls
parameter_group_params = {
  immediate = {
    autovacuum         = 1
    client_encoding    = "utf8"
    log_connections    = "1"
    log_disconnections = "1"
    log_statement      = "all"
  }
  pending-reboot = {
    shared_preload_libraries     = "pgaudit",
    track_activity_query_size    = "2048",
    "pgaudit.log"                = "ALL",
    "pgaudit.log_level"          = "info",
    "pgaudit.log_statement_once" = "1"
  }
}
```

> Parameters for pg_extension are `pending_reboot` parameters. It means that you need to reboot your instance to be effectivly applied. In our case, because there are defined at the deployment of the RDS Instance, it's not necessary to reboot. 

You can see the pgaudit logs directly from the rds api. Check the script `retrieve-audit-logs.sh`.

> Note the `grep AUDIT` will truncate the SQL queries that are on several lines.

## SOC & Indexation Logs

Because those logs are managed by cloudwatch logs, you can monitor them by indexing on an **elasticsearch** or any other stacks that supports cloudwatch logs.

For demonstration purposes, you can achieve that by setting to `true` the variable `create_elasticsearch` available in the terraform.tfvars.

```
################################################
# ElasticSearch
################################################
create_elasticsearch = false
es_instance_type     = "t3.small.elasticsearch"
es_instance_count    = 1
es_ebs_volume_size   = 10
```

> As for RDS Instance, the elasticSearch domain endpoint is publicly accessible. A restriction is made on the domain policy to restrict access to the IP Addresses setted into `var.allowed_ip_addresses`.

You just have to subscribe the cloudwatch log group to the elasticsearch domain endpoint. You can do it directly from the console. Check this blog to do it in a clean way : 

https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/database/analyze-postgresql-logs-with-amazon-elasticsearch-service/

You can do it progammatically with the code available in `elasticsearch.tf` file : 

```
###########################################
# Deploy a subscription filter on RDS CloudWatch Logs
# to stream logs on an ElasticSearch domain endpoint
###########################################
module "stream2es" {
  source  = "jparnaudeau/cloudwatch-subscription-elasticsearch/aws"
  version = "1.0.0"

  for_each = var.create_elasticsearch ? toset(["1"]) : []

  # gloval variables
  region      = var.region
  environment = var.environment
  tags        = local.tags

  # other variables
  function_name           = local.lambda_function_name
  rds_name                = var.rds_name
  rds_cloudwatch_log_name = format("/aws/rds/instance/%s/postgresql", var.rds_name)
  es_domain_endpoint      = try(module.elasticsearch.domain_endpoint, "")
  source_account_id       = data.aws_caller_identity.current.account_id
  lambda_role_arn         = aws_iam_role.lambda-role.arn
}
```


> This module will deploy the official AWS Lambda function (the same that if you do it in the console) but with 2 little updates : the elasticsearch domain endpoint is pass threw a lambda environment variable and second, following best practices in elasticSearch, create one index per day.


At the end of your `terraform apply`, if you go on the kibana endpoint of your elasticsearch domain, you should see your audit logs.

> You can filter logs to retrieve queries on a particular table : `message:*AUDIT* and message:*customer*`

> You can filter logs to retrieve queries for a particular user : `message:*AUDIT* and misc:*batch*`

> in standard parameter of your PostgreSQL server, you can set `log_statement = all`. This directive is not enough in case of audit system. Each dynamic query made inside a plsql procedure are not logged. By using pgaudit, you can see in the elasticsearch index all queries executed.
